<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Alpha Kappa Alpha</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>Alpha Kappa Alpha</b> (<b>ΑΚΑ</b>) was the first <a href="/wiki/Greek_alphabet" title="Greek alphabet">Greek-lettered</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities_in_North_America" title="Fraternities and sororities in North America">sorority</a> established by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">African-American</a> college women. Membership is for college educated women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The sorority was founded on January 15, 1908, at <a href="/wiki/Howard_University" title="Howard University">Howard University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, by a group of sixteen students, led by <a href="/wiki/Ethel_Hedgeman_Lyle" title="Ethel Hedgeman Lyle">Ethel Hedgeman Lyle</a>. Forming a sorority broke barriers for African-American women in areas where little power or authority existed due to a lack of opportunities for minorities and women in the early 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Alpha Kappa Alpha was <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_(business)" title="Incorporation (business)">incorporated</a> on January 29, 1913.</p>
<p>Consisting of college-educated women of many diverse backgrounds from around the world, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_race" title="Black race">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_race" title="Caucasian race">Caucasian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> descent, the sorority serves through a membership of more than 283,000 women in 992 chapters in the United States and several other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AKAmember_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-AKAmember-6">[6]</a></sup> Women may join through undergraduate chapters at a college or university or they may also join through a graduate chapter after acquiring an undergraduate or advanced college degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AKAint_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-AKAint-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the organization's establishment, Alpha Kappa Alpha has helped to improve social and economic conditions through community service programs. Members have improved education through independent initiatives, contributed to community-building by creating programs and associations, such as the Mississippi Health Clinic, and influenced federal legislation by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress">Congressional</a> lobbying through the National Non-Partisan Lobby on Civil and Democratic Rights. The sorority works with communities through service initiatives and progressive programs relating to education, family, health, and business.</p>
<p>Alpha Kappa Alpha is part of the <a href="/wiki/National_Pan-Hellenic_Council" title="National Pan-Hellenic Council">National Pan-Hellenic Council</a> (NPHC). The current International President is Dorothy Buckhanan Wilson, and the sorority's document and pictorial archives are located at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moorland-Spingarn_Research_Center" title="Moorland-Spingarn Research Center">Moorland-Spingarn Research Center</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MainandMiner_Hall.GIF"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="241" data-file-width="367" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/58/MainandMiner_Hall.GIF/220px-MainandMiner_Hall.GIF" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/58/MainandMiner_Hall.GIF/330px-MainandMiner_Hall.GIF 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/58/MainandMiner_Hall.GIF 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MainandMiner_Hall.GIF" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Main Hall and Miner Hall in 1868. Miner Hall is located to the left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-minerhall_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-minerhall-8">[8]</a></sup> Miner Hall was the site of Alpha Kappa Alpha's founding on January 15, 1908.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lambdaeta-2_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-lambdaeta-2-9">[9]</a></sup> The building was demolished in 1961.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demolish_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-demolish-10">[10]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings:_1907.E2.80.931912">Beginnings: 1907–1912</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Beginnings: 1907–1912">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In spring 1907, Ethel Hedgeman led efforts to create a sisterhood at Howard University. Howard faculty member Ethal Robinson encouraged Hedgeman by relating her own observances of sorority life at the Women's College at <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a>, even though she was not a member of any sorority while a student at Brown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ross-166_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ross-166-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-delta_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-delta-12">[12]</a></sup> Hedgeman was also inspired by her mentors at Howard. To implement her idea, Hedgeman began recruiting interested classmates during the summer of 1907.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey19_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey19-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eventually, nine women including Hedgeman were instrumental in organizing Alpha Kappa Alpha in the fall of 1907.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ross-166_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ross-166-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey19_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey19-13">[13]</a></sup> With Hedgeman serving as the temporary chairperson,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-delta_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-delta-12">[12]</a></sup> the women wrote the sorority's constitution, devised the motto, chose the favorite colors, and named the sorority Alpha Kappa Alpha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ross-166_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ross-166-11">[11]</a></sup> Later in 1908, seven sophomore <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honor_student" title="Honor student">honor students</a> expressed interest in joining and were accepted without initiation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ross-166_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ross-166-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parker12_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parker12-14">[14]</a></sup> The first initiation was held in a wing of Miner Hall on Howard University on February 11, 1909.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lambdaeta-1_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-lambdaeta-1-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akatimeline_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-akatimeline-16">[16]</a></sup> On May 25, 1909, Alpha Kappa Alpha held its first "Ivy Week," a celebration that included planting ivy at Miner Hall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VCU_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-VCU-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Struggles_and_incorporation:_1912.E2.80.931913">Struggles and incorporation: 1912–1913</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Struggles and incorporation: 1912–1913">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AKAcertificate.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="432" data-file-width="600" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/AKAcertificate.jpg/200px-AKAcertificate.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/AKAcertificate.jpg/300px-AKAcertificate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/AKAcertificate.jpg/400px-AKAcertificate.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AKAcertificate.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A 1921 Certificate of Membership from the <a href="/wiki/Gamma" title="Gamma">Gamma</a> Chapter at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana-Champaign" title="University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign">University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akatimeline_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-akatimeline-16">[16]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Alpha Kappa Alpha continued to grow at Howard. By the end of the 1911–12 school year, there were more than twenty members of the sorority and the organization had become an influential part of student life at Howard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Following the annual celebration "Ivy Day" on Howard campus in Spring 1912, founder and former Basileus Nellie Quander learned that several other newly initiated members of the sorority planned to change the colors, letters, and constitution of the sorority, and to make it more active outside Howard University. On January 13, 1913, the entire twenty-two-member undergraduate chapter voted to transform the original Alpha Kappa Alpha into <a href="/wiki/Delta_Sigma_Theta" title="Delta Sigma Theta">Delta Sigma Theta</a>. Quander actively worked to maintain the integrity and tenets of Alpha Kappa Alpha. She, along with the women who had become ΑΚΑs during the four years of the sorority's existence who had since graduated, elected to remain Alpha Kappa Alpha. Quander set up a three-person committee that successfully petitioned to incorporate ΑΚΑ as a perpetual entity. Alpha Kappa Alpha was nationally incorporated on January 29, 1913.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BadgeAKA2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="968" data-file-width="810" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/BadgeAKA2.jpg/150px-BadgeAKA2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/BadgeAKA2.jpg/225px-BadgeAKA2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/BadgeAKA2.jpg/300px-BadgeAKA2.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BadgeAKA2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A close up of an <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Alpha" title="Alpha Phi Alpha">Alpha Phi Alpha</a> delegate badge from the 23rd Boulé. The tri-convention—consisting of Alpha Kappa Alpha, Alpha Phi Alpha, and <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Psi" title="Kappa Alpha Psi">Kappa Alpha Psi</a>—was held from December 27, through 31, 1940 in <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri" title="Kansas City, Missouri">Kansas City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akatimeline_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-akatimeline-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_and_implementation_of_programs:_1913.E2.80.931940">Expansion and implementation of programs: 1913–1940</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Expansion and implementation of programs: 1913–1940">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alpha Kappa Alpha continued to grow nationally. A second chapter at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a> was chartered in fall 1913.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> In addition, Alpha Kappa Alpha helped to support members by providing scholarship funds for school and foreign studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Alpha Kappa Alpha began to unite members at the annual <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Alpha#Boul.C3.A9" title="Alpha Kappa Alpha">Boulé</a>, the sorority's governing body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akaterms_2-7"><a href="#cite_note-akaterms-2">[2]</a></sup> The sorority's pledge was written by Grace Edwards and was adopted by the 1920 Boulé.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcnealey329_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-mcnealey329-1">[1]</a></sup> In addition, the sorority's crest was designed by Phyllis Wheatley Waters and accepted in the same Boulé.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcnealey329_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-mcnealey329-1">[1]</a></sup> A year later, at the 1921 Boulé, the <i>Ivy Leaf</i> was designated as "the official organ of Alpha Kappa Alpha," and Founders' Week, paying honor to ΆKΆ's founders was established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcnealey329_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-mcnealey329-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ross167_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ross167-23">[23]</a></sup> Pearls were first introduced to the sorority in the same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcnealey329_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-mcnealey329-1">[1]</a></sup> The sorority membership pin was accepted in the following Boulé in <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri" title="Kansas City, Missouri">Kansas City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Midwestern_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Midwestern-24">[24]</a></sup> At the 1947 Boulé, pins for honorary members were designed and approved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcnealey327_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-mcnealey327-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 10, 1930, Alpha Kappa Alpha, along with the fraternities <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Psi" title="Kappa Alpha Psi">Kappa Alpha Psi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Omega_Psi_Phi" title="Omega Psi Phi">Omega Psi Phi</a> and sororities Delta Sigma Theta and <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Phi_Beta" title="Zeta Phi Beta">Zeta Phi Beta</a>, formed the <a href="/wiki/National_Pan-Hellenic_Council" title="National Pan-Hellenic Council">National Pan-Hellenic Council</a> (NPHC) at Howard University.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPHC_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-NPHC-26">[26]</a></sup> Currently consisting of nine predominately black fraternities and sororities, NPHC promotes interaction through forums, meetings, and other mediums for the exchange of information, and engages in cooperative programming and initiatives through various activities and functions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPHC_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-NPHC-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ivyleaf.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="432" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Ivyleaf.jpg/140px-Ivyleaf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Ivyleaf.jpg/210px-Ivyleaf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Ivyleaf.jpg/280px-Ivyleaf.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ivyleaf.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A 1934 issue of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivy" title="Ivy">Ivy Leaf</a></i>, Alpha Kappa Alpha's official organ<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akaterms_2-8"><a href="#cite_note-akaterms-2">[2]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Throughout the <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">Great Migration</a>, members assisted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Travelers_Aid_Society" title="Travelers Aid Society">Travelers Aid Society</a>, to help thousands of <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern</a> Blacks adjust to <a href="/wiki/Northern_United_States" title="Northern United States">Northern</a> society, find housing and navigate around the city. They also volunteered at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedman%27s_Hospital" title="Freedman's Hospital">Freedman's Hospital</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ross167_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ross167-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 1933, during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, International President Ida Jackson visited All Saints Industrial School in <a href="/wiki/Lexington,_Mississippi" title="Lexington, Mississippi">Lexington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>. She found difficult conditions in the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_Delta" title="Mississippi Delta">Mississippi Delta</a>. Some of the teachers did not have an education past the seventh grade. African Americans were trying to make a living sharecropping on plantation land as agricultural prices continued to fall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OLDMISS_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-OLDMISS-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nealey150_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-nealey150-28">[28]</a></sup> In summer 1934, Ida Jackson initiated the Summer School for Rural Teachers to train future teachers. She worked with a total of 22 student teachers and 243 school children. In addition, she held night classes for 48 adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nealey151_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-nealey151-29">[29]</a></sup> By obtaining 2600 books for the school's library, Jackson made it "the largest library owned by white or colored in all Holmes County."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nealey151_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-nealey151-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>In summer 1938, Ida Jackson focused on poverty and established a regional health clinic. She had acquired $1,000 from the Boulé to fund the project in December 1935.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nealey181_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-nealey181-30">[30]</a></sup> The clinic evolved into the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mississippi_Health_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mississippi Health Project (page does not exist)">Mississippi Health Project</a>, with Dr. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dorothy_Boulding_Ferebee" title="Dorothy Boulding Ferebee">Dorothy Boulding Ferebee</a> appointed as the director.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nealey181_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-nealey181-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Mississippi Health Project brought primary medical care to the rural Black population across the state for six summers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIH-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup> The program has been recognized as the first mobile health clinic in the United States, assisting approximately 15,000 people in the Mississippi Delta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parker87_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-parker87-33">[33]</a></sup> The project was noted for helping to decrease cases <a href="/wiki/Diphtheria" title="Diphtheria">diphtheria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> in the region and to improve nutritional and dental practices throughout rural Mississippi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Balance_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Balance-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PLEAID_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-PLEAID-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Led by incorporator Norma Elizabeth Boyd, the sorority created the National Non-Partisan Lobby on Civil and Democratic Rights (NPC) in 1938, later renamed the National Non-Partisan Council on Public Affairs. It was the first full-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress">congressional</a> <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">lobby</a> for minority group civil rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nealey157_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-nealey157-37">[37]</a></sup> Throughout the organization's life, the Non-Partisan Council worked with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAACP" title="NAACP">NAACP</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Urban_League" title="National Urban League">National Urban League</a>, The United Office and Professional Workers of America, The National Association of Graduate Nurses, the American Federation of Churches, the Colored Women's Club, the Brotherhood of Sleeping Car Porters and Auxiliary, and the New York Voter's League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parker195_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parker195-38">[38]</a></sup> The NPC was dissolved on July 15, 1948, by twelfth Supreme Basileus Edna Over Gray-Campbell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nealey157_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-nealey157-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nealey157_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-nealey157-37">[37]</a></sup> A year later, Alpha Kappa Alpha was the first sorority to apply for life membership in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAACP" title="NAACP">NAACP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>To replace the NPC, in August 1945, Alpha Kappa Alpha established the American Council on Human Rights (ACHR). The council made recommendations to the government concerning <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_rights" title="Civil rights">civil rights</a> legislation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCNeal158_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-MCNeal158-40">[40]</a></sup> The ACHR was proposed at the 1946 Boulé.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCNeal158_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-MCNeal158-40">[40]</a></sup> In October 1946, Alpha Kappa Alpha was the first sorority to obtain observer status at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> On January 25, 1948, Delta Sigma Theta, Zeta Phi Beta, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Gamma_Rho" title="Sigma Gamma Rho">Sigma Gamma Rho</a> sororities and Alpha Phi Alpha and <a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Sigma" title="Phi Beta Sigma">Phi Beta Sigma</a> fraternities were charter members of the ACHR.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCNeal159_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-MCNeal159-42">[42]</a></sup> Kappa Alpha Psi later was included in March 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCNeal160_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-MCNeal160-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parker101_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-parker101-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 1, 1945, Alpha Kappa Alpha established The National Health Office in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parker87_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-parker87-33">[33]</a></sup> The National Health Office coordinated activities with local chapters and worked with the ACHC to promote health initiatives before <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress">Congress</a>, increase the number of student <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nurse" title="Nurse">nurses</a>, and improve the state of health programs at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HBCU" title="HBCU">historically Black Colleges and Universities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parker88_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-parker88-45">[45]</a></sup> The National Health Office was dissolved in 1951, as its goals were incorporated into the sorority's international program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parker89_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-parker89-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_rights_and_educational_training:_1950.E2.80.931970">Civil rights and educational training: 1950–1970</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Civil rights and educational training: 1950–1970">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Throughout the 1950s, 1960s, and 1970s, members helped to sponsor job training, reading enrichment, heritage and youth programs. By encouraging youth to improve math, science, and reading skills, the sorority continued a legacy of community service and pledged to enrich the lives of others. Financially, Alpha Kappa Alpha expanded funding for projects in 1953 through the creation and trademark of a fashion show called Fashionetta<sup>TM</sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcnealey327_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-mcnealey327-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AKADBO_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-AKADBO-47">[47]</a></sup> Politically, ACHR continued lobbying for equality concerning civil rights during the 1950s and 1960s. According to Collier-Thomas, the ACHR drew attention to legislation concerning education, transportation, employment, and improving equality in the <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a> and public places.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The ACHR participated in filing civil rights cases in <a href="/wiki/Amicus_curiae" title="Amicus curiae">amicus curiae</a> with <i><a href="/wiki/Bolling_v._Sharpe" title="Bolling v. Sharpe">Bolling v. Sharpe</a></i> and 1954's <i><a href="/wiki/Brown_v._Board_of_Education" title="Brown v. Board of Education">Brown v. Board of Education</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IvyLeafArch_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-IvyLeafArch-49">[49]</a></sup> However, as a whole, ACHR voted to dissolve operations in 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IvyLeafArch_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-IvyLeafArch-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alpha Kappa Alpha contributed programs for inner city youth by capitalizing on political gains in the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>. On August 20, 1964, President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_Johnson" title="Lyndon Johnson">Lyndon Johnson</a> signed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_Opportunity_Act" title="Economic Opportunity Act">Economic Opportunity Act</a>, which allowed the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Job_Corps" title="Job Corps">Job Corps</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey132_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey132-50">[50]</a></sup> The sorority wanted to operate a job training center for students. Led by president Julia Purnell, ΆKΆ negotiated with the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Economic_Opportunity" title="Office of Economic Opportunity">Office of Economic Opportunity</a> to operate a women's center from October 1964 to January 1965.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey132_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey132-50">[50]</a></sup> Alpha Kappa Alpha was awarded a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a>4 million grant to operate the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio" title="Cleveland, Ohio">Cleveland</a> Job Corps on February 12, 1965, becoming the first sorority to operate a federal job training center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey132_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey132-50">[50]</a></sup> Beginning in 1965, the Cleveland Job Corps trained female high school dropouts, aged 16 to 21, with job and educational skills. In 1976, the Cleveland Job Corps accepted males.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup> The sorority operated the Cleveland Job Corps until 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clevelandencyclopedia_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-clevelandencyclopedia-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The sorority educated the community through highlighting the accomplishments of notable individuals by publishing <i>The Heritage Series</i> between 1968 and 1972.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akatimeline_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-akatimeline-16">[16]</a></sup> These <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pamphlets" title="Pamphlets">pamphlets</a> were a series of biographies of top African-American women. Altogether, the entire collection contained "Women in the <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judiciary</a>," "Women in <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">Politics</a>," "Women in <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">Medicine</a>," "Women in <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">Business</a>," and "Women in <a href="/wiki/Dentistry" title="Dentistry">Dentistry</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pamphlet_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-pamphlet-52">[52]</a></sup> Alpha Kappa Alpha also donated $20,000 for preserving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr.,_National_Historic_Site#King_Birth_Home" title="Martin Luther King, Jr., National Historic Site">birthplace</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, in the early 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> In 1978, during the sorority's seventieth anniversary, the Memorial Window at Howard University was dedicated to the founders of Alpha Kappa Alpha. Surviving founders Lavinia Norman and Norma Boyd attended the celebration of unveiling the Memorial Window, designed by Lois Mailou Jones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McN330_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-McN330-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bridging_toward_the_twenty-first_century:_1980.E2.80.932007">Bridging toward the twenty-first century: 1980–2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Bridging toward the twenty-first century: 1980–2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Soon after the sorority's 75th anniversary, Alpha Kappa Alpha contributed funds to decrease Africa's poverty with the establishment of African Village Development Program (AVDP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey185_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey185-55">[55]</a></sup> As a conjoint program with <a href="/wiki/Africare" title="Africare">Africare</a>, the sorority sought to decrease poverty in African villages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey185_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey185-55">[55]</a></sup> In collaboration with the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=International_Foundation_for_Education_and_Self-Help&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="International Foundation for Education and Self-Help (page does not exist)">International Foundation for Education and Self-Help</a> (IFESH), the sorority built ten schools in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> after <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> ended, and it donated computer technology to the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-4"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey186_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey186-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout the 1990s, the sorority continued to provide after-school mentoring programs, such as ON TRACK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-5"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup> ON TRACK, an acronym which stands for "Organizing, Nurturing, Team building, Respecting, Achieving, Counseling and Knowing," was designed to help the progress of 20,000 third graders who were at-risk of failing their education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey153_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey153-57">[57]</a></sup> Sponsored by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daimler_Chrysler" title="Daimler Chrysler">Daimler Chrysler</a>, ON TRACK was designated to "improve communication, academics, physical and emotional health, peer leadership, etiquette, and interpersonal relationships."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-6"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey153_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey153-57">[57]</a></sup> In addition, programs such as the Ivy Reading AKAdemy and Young Authors Program improved elementary reading comprehension skills, while P.I.M.S. highlighted programs in math and science.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-7"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nih_aka3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="252" data-file-width="371" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Nih_aka3.jpg/240px-Nih_aka3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Nih_aka3.jpg/360px-Nih_aka3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Nih_aka3.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nih_aka3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Acting Surgeon General Rear Admiral <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_P._Moritsugu" title="Kenneth P. Moritsugu">Kenneth P. Moritsugu</a> addressing participants at the Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority, Incorporated's 98th National Founders Day in 2006. Then Alpha Kappa Alpha Executive Director Barbara McKinzie sits to the right.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIHFD_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIHFD-58">[58]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:38%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>The purpose of Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority is to cultivate and encourage high scholastic and ethical standards, to promote unity and friendship among college women, to study and help alleviate problems concerning girls and women in order to improve their social stature, to maintain a progressive interest in college life, and to be of service to all mankind.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">Sorority Creed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-purpose_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-purpose-59">[59]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>The sorority responded to the call for help in fall 2005 after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>, by raising money for a disaster relief fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey185_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey185-55">[55]</a></sup> In July 2007, through <a href="/wiki/Habitat_for_Humanity" title="Habitat for Humanity">Habitat for Humanity</a>, the sorority helped build a house in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> for a family that survived Hurricane Katrina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewOrleans_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-NewOrleans-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to educational programs, Alpha Kappa Alpha contributed to drawing awareness to health-related issues, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS">AIDS</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sickle_cell_anemia" title="Sickle cell anemia">sickle cell anemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breast_cancer" title="Breast cancer">breast cancer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">the importance of staying in shape</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey185_55-3"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey185-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pounds_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-pounds-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cwelcome_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-cwelcome-62">[62]</a></sup> Recently, the sorority has supported the efforts of justice for the <a href="/wiki/Jena_Six" title="Jena Six">Jena Six</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jena6_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jena6-63">[63]</a></sup> Also, the sorority connects to the past by partnering with African Ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Sorority members may use African Ancestry's <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> testing to find <a href="/wiki/Genealogical_DNA_test#United_States_-_African_ancestry" title="Genealogical DNA test">genealogical</a> data for themselves and their families. The purpose of the partnership is to help members trace family connections through the world as well as in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, to embrace African-American culture and the larger community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dna_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-dna-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Centennial_celebration:_2008">Centennial celebration: 2008</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Centennial celebration: 2008">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alpha Kappa Alpha celebrated its centenary with a year-long commemoration in 2008. The celebration coincided with the sorority's biennial Boulé.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Centennial_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Centennial-66">[66]</a></sup> Internationally, some Alpha Kappa Alpha members began marking the festivities by making a <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage" title="Pilgrimage">pilgrimage</a> to Howard University from January 12 to January 15, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Centennial_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Centennial-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pilgrim_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-pilgrim-67">[67]</a></sup> The activities included sorority members financially donating $1 million in scholarship funds to Howard University,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> contributing libraries for Middle School for Mathematics and Science and Asbury Dwelling for Senior Citizens, and unveiling a digital version of the entire <i>Ivy Leaf</i> publication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In addition, sorority undergraduate and graduate members who were not available to attend ceremonies in Washington, D.C., held celebrations in local cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> On July 11 to July 18, 2008, Alpha Kappa Alpha held their 63rd Boulé. A town hall meeting with the public, a unity march in conjunction with other NPHC members, and a concert featuring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winning singer <a href="/wiki/Patti_LaBelle" title="Patti LaBelle">Patti LaBelle</a> were some of the events which occurred at the centennial Boulé.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> On July 17, 2008, Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority set a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Record" title="Guinness World Record">Guinness World Record</a> when 16,206 members set a record by having the largest-ever silver service sit-down dinner in a convention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Akamuseumcropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="800" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Akamuseumcropped.jpg/200px-Akamuseumcropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Akamuseumcropped.jpg/300px-Akamuseumcropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Akamuseumcropped.jpg/400px-Akamuseumcropped.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akamuseumcropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ΑΚΑ's centennial museum at the <a href="/wiki/Walter_E._Washington_Convention_Center" title="Walter E. Washington Convention Center">Walter E. Washington Convention Center</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Alpha Kappa Alpha's accomplishments were heralded by the United States Congress, with <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> and sorority member <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. Representative</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sheila_Jackson-Lee" title="Sheila Jackson-Lee">Sheila Jackson-Lee</a>, who both agreed to pass legislation in both houses of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> to commemorate the sorority's founding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In addition, the toy company <a href="/wiki/Mattel" title="Mattel">Mattel</a> designed a <a href="/wiki/Barbie" title="Barbie">Barbie</a> collectible doll fashioned with a pink and green evening gown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuits.2C_forensic_audits.2C_and_IRS_review_of_former_president">Lawsuits, forensic audits, and IRS review of former president</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Lawsuits, forensic audits, and IRS review of former president">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On June 20, 2009, eight Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority members filed a complaint in D.C. Superior Court demanding that International President Barbara McKinzie be fired for improper use of sorority funds and the money be returned to the sorority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The lawsuit claimed that Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority, Incorporated's Executive Board approved the spending of substantial amounts on McKinzie's costs of living, including commissioning an expensive wax model of McKinzie. In response, McKinzie denied the allegations, describing them as "without merit." The memberships of the eight AKAs who filed the complaint were revoked by the sorority in retaliation for the lawsuit but later forced to be reinstated by a judge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2010, the Superior Court of the District of Columbia dismissed the lawsuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> On August 18, 2011, the District of Columbia Court of Appeals reversed the previous decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 22, 2012, a forensic audit of Alpha Kappa Alpha's 2010 financial records revealed troubling concerns with past president, Barbara McKinzie's development and access to a "secret" bank account. The audit of the sorority led to findings that supported the claims in the previous lawsuit. The audit also found two former officials continued to use sorority credit cards after their service ended, failing to appropriately document charges. Another lawsuit against the organization, the former president McKinzie and other officials contained similar allegations. The audit found that McKinzie and the other officials secretly created a second set of financial books to get around the sorority's accounting policies. According to the audit, "(n)early $1.7 million in payments were made to the former president, Barbara McKinzie, without authorization. Approximately $282,000 in credit card charges on a second set of books appear to be fraudulent, including personal charges the sorority wasn't reimbursed for."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Audit_pdf_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Audit_pdf-86">[86]</a></sup> Barbara McKinzie later was expelled from the sorority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also the sorority's tax returns were audited by the Internal Revenue Service. The audit was expected to be concluded sometime in January 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Audit_pdf_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Audit_pdf-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CSULA_hazing_death_lawsuit">CSULA hazing death lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: CSULA hazing death lawsuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On September 9, 2002, pledges Kristin High (22 years old mother of one) and Kenitha Saafir (24 years old) from <a href="/wiki/California_State_University,_Los_Angeles" title="California State University, Los Angeles">California State University – Los Angeles</a> (CSULA), were pronounced dead as a result of an illegal and dangerous pledging ritual. The women were instructed by members of Alpha Kappa Alpha to perform a series of activities blindfolded on Dockweiler State Beach when a high tide came and eventually drowned both of them. The next day when sorority members brought Kristin's car and cellphone to her mother, she noticed Kristin's pledge journal suddenly missing from her car and numbers deleted from her cellphone. Prior to Kristin's death, Kristin's mother encouraged her to fully disassociate herself from the sorority after Kristin discussed the unsisterly behavior displayed by members of AKA such as disrespecting pledges and forcing them to run late night errands for AKA members. A year after the tragic incident, the families of the deceased settled with Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority Incorporated after filing a $100 million wrongful death lawsuit. The sorority initially denied having an active chapter at CSULA in an effort to deny responsibility for the deaths but the court dismissed their claim and held the whole sorority accountable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alpha_Chapter_hazing_lawsuit">Alpha Chapter hazing lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Alpha Chapter hazing lawsuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two Howard University seniors filed a lawsuit against Alpha Kappa Alpha Incorporated in 2013. The women accused the sorority of barring them from membership through the most prestigious chapter of the sorority, Alpha Chapter, despite being "legacies" (their mothers are Alpha Chapter initiates of the sorority) and in retaliation for exposing illegal hazing. The mothers initially had their AKA memberships revoked for supporting their daughters in the litigation process against the sorority, months later a judge reinstated their memberships citing that it was illegal for AKA to revoke their paid memberships for simply filing a lawsuit against their own sorority. In the lawsuit, the two students stated as prospective members of the Alpha Chapter they were verbally abused by women of the sorority, could not wear sorority colors or any colors that could be blended into pink or green, they could not wear pearls, they were forced to run errands and buy items for sorority members, they could not socialize with their non-AKA friends, they were often humiliated in front of other students, they could not eat at a popular lunch spot on campus, they could not use the same doors as sorority members, and at one point they had to call their "big sisters" daily or suffer some type of consequence. The women were denied their only opportunity to join the Alpha Chapter before they graduated because the chapter was suspended from bringing in new members following an investigation of hazing allegations their previous eligible years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership">Membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Alpha_Kappa_Alpha_sisters" title="List of Alpha Kappa Alpha sisters">List of Alpha Kappa Alpha sisters</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AKAheadquarters.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="590" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/AKAheadquarters.jpg/240px-AKAheadquarters.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/AKAheadquarters.jpg/360px-AKAheadquarters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/AKAheadquarters.jpg/480px-AKAheadquarters.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AKAheadquarters.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alpha Kappa Alpha's National Headquarters in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" title="Chicago, Illinois">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Alpha Kappa Alpha reports a membership of over 283,000 women internationally. The sorority has over 65,000 active members with many different backgrounds and professions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-members_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-members-3">[3]</a></sup> Graduate members constitute the largest percentage of membership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AKAmember_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-AKAmember-6">[6]</a></sup> Alpha Kappa Alpha has 992 chapters, located in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>The term <i>soror</i>, derived from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for "sister",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> is used between members of the sorority. Membership of the Directorate includes the Board of Directors. For graduate chapters, "<a href="/wiki/Omega" title="Omega">Omega</a>" is added to distinguish those which consist of college graduates from undergraduate chapters. "Supreme," as a term, is preposed to the title of an international officeholder, such as <i>Supreme Basileus</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akaterms_2-9"><a href="#cite_note-akaterms-2">[2]</a></sup> Deceased members are referred to as "Ivies Beyond the Wall".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akaterms_2-10"><a href="#cite_note-akaterms-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Honorary membership<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> is Alpha Kappa Alpha's highest honor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AKAmember_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-AKAmember-6">[6]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Addams" title="Jane Addams">Jane Addams</a>, winner of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>, is among the first honorary members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parker-272_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-parker-272-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/First_Lady" title="First Lady">First Lady</a> and wife of <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>, was made an honorary member. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>, former Senator and First Lady, and wife of President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, accepted honorary membership into Alpha Kappa Alpha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hillary_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-hillary-94">[94]</a></sup> However, Clinton later declined initiation into the organization due to the sorority's exclusive requirement preventing acceptance into other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NPHC" title="NPHC">Pan-Hellenic</a> organizations, and desired her membership in Alpha Kappa Alpha to be "non-exclusive."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hillary_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-hillary-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celebrate_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-celebrate-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership_interest_and_intake">Membership interest and intake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Membership interest and intake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Ivy Leaf Pledge Club was the official pledge club of Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority, Incorporated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Potential candidates who were interested in joining the sorority would join the pledge club before being inducted into the sorority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LZ_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-LZ-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ivyleafclub.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="335" data-file-width="468" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Ivyleafclub.jpg/200px-Ivyleafclub.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Ivyleafclub.jpg/300px-Ivyleafclub.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Ivyleafclub.jpg/400px-Ivyleafclub.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ivyleafclub.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An "Ivy Leaf Pledge Club" located at <a href="/wiki/Wilberforce_University" title="Wilberforce University">Wilberforce University</a> in 1922</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <i>Our Kind of People: Inside America's Upper Class,</i> <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Otis_Graham" title="Lawrence Otis Graham">Lawrence Otis Graham</a> tells of his aunt's experience in joining the Ivy Pledge Club:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">We had to learn a lot more about the historic beginnings of the AKAs, and we did it by writing long letters of application to the Ivy Leaf Pledge Club—the senior wing of the sorority that regulated the admissions process—and then attending monthly meetings where the older students tutored us on the history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-log_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-log-98">[98]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In addition, according to Graham, the sorority would have "Pledge Week", a period where a candidate's grades and behavior were reviewed by chapter members. Candidates who withstood this period were initiated into the sorority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-log_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-log-98">[98]</a></sup> Membership interest is processed by an interest meeting, known as a "rush". After the candidate receives an official letter from the sorority, she can participate in the membership intake process. Prospective members must have a C+ average or better prior to their membership submission, as well as a record of community service. If a prospective member has graduated, that member could be invited to join the sorority at the discretion of the graduate chapter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prospective_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-prospective-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership:_founders_and_executive_directors">Leadership: founders and executive directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Leadership: founders and executive directors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The leadership of the sorority in the early years was derived from three separate groups—the original group, the sophomores and the incorporators, who together were known as "The Twenty Pearls."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akaterms_2-11"><a href="#cite_note-akaterms-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AKA-Leaders_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-AKA-Leaders-100">[100]</a></sup> The Executive Director position has been held by eight members since the office's creation on October 9, 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boul.C3.A9">Boulé</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Boulé">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Alpha_Kappa_Alpha_Boul%C3%A9s" title="List of Alpha Kappa Alpha Boulés">List of Alpha Kappa Alpha Boulés</a></div>
<p>The Boulé<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[A]</a></sup> is the regulating institution of the sorority and currently meets every two years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akaterms_2-12"><a href="#cite_note-akaterms-2">[2]</a></sup> Throughout the years, notable individuals such as civil rights activists Martin Luther King, Jr. and <a href="/wiki/Roy_Wilkins" title="Roy Wilkins">Roy Wilkins</a> were speakers at past Boulé conferences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akatimeline_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-akatimeline-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Akaregion.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="552" data-file-width="800" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Akaregion.gif/200px-Akaregion.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Akaregion.gif/300px-Akaregion.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Akaregion.gif/400px-Akaregion.gif 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akaregion.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The nine regions of Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority within the United States<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regions2_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-regions2-108">[107]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the establishment of 32 graduate and undergraduate chapters in 1924, Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority organized chapters according to their regions in the United States and abroad. The Boulé determines the boundaries of the regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regions_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-regions-109">[108]</a></sup> The ten regions are each led by a regional director, where she serves a member of the sorority's Board of Directors. In addition to serving on the sorority's Board of Directors, the regional director also follows guidelines, program targets set by the International President, as well as procedures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regions_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-regions-109">[108]</a></sup> Almost two-thirds of the sorority's regional directors have been elected international presidents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regions_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-regions-109">[108]</a></sup> A comprehensive list of regions is shown below:</p>
<div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style='"border-collapse:'>
<tr>
<td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.akafarwest.com/Welcome.html" rel="nofollow">Far-Western</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.akamidwestern.com/" rel="nofollow">Mid-Western</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110511180537/http://www.aka-southcentralregion.com/akascr/" rel="nofollow">South Central</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.akacentral.org/" rel="nofollow">Central</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.akasoutheastern.org/" rel="nofollow">South Eastern</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.akasouthatlanticregion.org/" rel="nofollow">South Atlantic</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.midatlanticaka.org/" rel="nofollow">Mid-Atlantic</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://akanorthatlantic.org/" rel="nofollow">North Atlantic</a></li>

<li>International</li>
</ul>
