</tr>
</table>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_programs">National programs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: National programs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Educational_Advancement_Foundation">Educational Advancement Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Educational Advancement Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alpha Kappa Alpha's Educational Advancement Foundation (EAF) is a separate and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tax-exempt" title="Tax-exempt">tax-exempt</a> branch of the sorority, which "provide[s] financial support to individuals and organizations engaged in lifelong learning."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aboutEAF_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-aboutEAF-110">[109]</a></sup> The foundation awards academic scholarships (for undergraduate members of the sorority, as well as non-members), <a href="/wiki/Fellow" title="Fellow">fellowships</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grant_(money)" title="Grant (money)">grants</a> for community service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PASEAF_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-PASEAF-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="History_and_donations">History and donations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: History and donations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The foundation was the brainchild of Constance Holland, the sister of former Alpha Kappa Alpha International President Dr. Barbara Phillips, in 1978. The foundation had official beginnings in 1980 and the sorority donated US$10,000 for the project. Eight years later, the organization first awarded $10,000 to fourteen students. In 1991, EAF first awarded mini-grants to community organizations. In 1998, EAF provided the first Youth Partners Accessing Capital (PAC) award to an undergraduate member.</p>
<p>At the organization's twentieth anniversary in 2000, EAF published <i>Perpetuating Our Posterity: A Blueprint for Excellence.</i> The book served as a comprehensive history of the organization and as a source of advice for other beginning philanthropies. EAF went online with a <a href="/wiki/Website" title="Website">website</a> in 2003.</p>
<p>The organization celebrated a silver anniversary in <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau, Bahamas</a>, in 2005. EAF is incorporated into International President Barbara A. McKinzie's centennial program for funding under <b>E</b>xcellent <b>S</b>cholarly <b>P</b>erformance. Overall, EAF has donated more than $200,000 in grants and awarded 1,400 students with scholarships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AKAEAF_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-AKAEAF-112">[111]</a></sup> Other major donors to EAF include <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">Continental Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Trust" title="Northern Trust">Northern Trust</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-donorsEAF_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-donorsEAF-113">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Projects">Projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AKAcommunityservice.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1108" data-file-width="713" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/AKAcommunityservice.jpg/150px-AKAcommunityservice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/AKAcommunityservice.jpg/225px-AKAcommunityservice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/AKAcommunityservice.jpg/300px-AKAcommunityservice.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AKAcommunityservice.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Members of Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority, Incorporated assisting <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>'s Department of Highway Safety in distributing booster seats to low income children</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b>Advocates for Black Colleges</b> – The purpose of the Advocates for Black Colleges is to raise $100,000 for a selected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HBCU" title="HBCU">historically black college and university</a>, to support the institution's scholarships and program grants. Corporations as well as minority graduates of historically black colleges are encouraged to donate funds as well. The first college receiving aid is <a href="/wiki/Stillman_College" title="Stillman College">Stillman College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tuscaloosa,_Alabama" title="Tuscaloosa, Alabama">Tuscaloosa, Alabama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NI_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-NI-114">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Howard University Fund</b> – Alpha Kappa Alpha is celebrating the centennial of the sorority's founding by donating $2 million to Howard University though two facets. First, the Moorland-Spingarn Research Center houses the historical artifacts, photographs, documents, and recordings of Alpha Kappa Alpha's contributions to community service. One million dollars will be used to improve Alpha Kappa Alpha's archives. In addition, one million dollars will be donated to the Nellie M. Quander Scholarship Fund. The fund will be used to finance partial or full scholarships for Howard University women in their junior and senior years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NI_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-NI-114">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Chapter Scholarships</b> – Undergraduate and graduate members of Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority's chapters send separate dues to the Educational Advancement Foundation to fund local scholarships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NI_114-2"><a href="#cite_note-NI-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guidelines_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-guidelines-115">[114]</a></sup> Depending on the size of the contributions by the chapter, the scholarships generally range from $100 to $500. For a chapter to donate under the EAF's Endowment Fund, a chapter needs to raise $20,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memorandum_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-memorandum-116">[115]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><b>The Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority Traveling Exhibit</b> chronicles achievements of Alpha Kappa Alpha members through the organization's one-hundred years. The exhibit appears in several cities across the nation from 2006 to 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EAF_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-EAF-117">[116]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ivy_Acres">Ivy Acres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Ivy Acres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ivy Acres will be a retirement center located in <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem,_North_Carolina" title="Winston-Salem, North Carolina">Winston-Salem, North Carolina</a>. The retirement center is sponsored by Senior Residences, Incorporated, a subsidiary of Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-business_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-business-118">[117]</a></sup> Ivy Acres will be one of the first retirement centers founded by African-Americans and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minorities" title="Minorities">minorities</a> in the United States. It will offer assisted or individual living for individuals who are over fifty-five, regardless of background, ethnicity or religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-business_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-business-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-midatlantic_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-midatlantic-119">[118]</a></sup> Barbara K. Phillips, former Vice-President and Project Coordinator for Senior Residences, Incorporated, explains the purpose of Ivy Acres, "We determined that there is a need out there, but this will be open to all. We want to be diverse, we want to be multicultural. Anyone who wants to come will be welcome."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-business_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-business-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>The gated community will be located on a 48-acre (190,000 m<sup>2</sup>) site. The planning for Ivy Acres cost approximately $32 million USD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-business_118-3"><a href="#cite_note-business-118">[117]</a></sup> In addition, according to <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Wire" title="Business Wire">Business Wire</a></i>, Ivy Acres will comprise "188 independent residential units, which will be both apartments and cottages, forty assisted-living apartments and twenty private accommodations for skilled nursing care."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-business_118-4"><a href="#cite_note-business-118">[117]</a></sup> Residents are expected to pay $1,890 to $2,890 per month for services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-business_118-5"><a href="#cite_note-business-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alphaepsilon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="310" height="310" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Alphaepsilon.jpg/200px-Alphaepsilon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Alphaepsilon.jpg/300px-Alphaepsilon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c5/Alphaepsilon.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alphaepsilon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alpha Kappa Alpha's Alpha Epsilon chapter at <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_University" title="Virginia State University">Virginia State University</a> in 1994.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ivy_Reading_AKAdemy">Ivy Reading AKAdemy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ivy Reading AKAdemy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Ivy Reading AKAdemy provides programs that encourage the entire community to become involved. The concept serves as an educational and human resource center for programs provided by Alpha Kappa Alpha. Working with <a href="/wiki/No_Child_Left_Behind_Act" title="No Child Left Behind Act">No Child Left Behind</a> in mind, "The Ivy Reading AKAdemy," a reading initiative, focuses on early learning and mastery of basic reading skills by the end of third grade. The Ivy Reading AKAdemy has a $1.5 million proposal pending with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Education" title="United States Department of Education">United States Department of Education</a> to fund a three-year nationwide after-school demonstration project in low-performing, economically deprived inner city schools in 16 sites within the continental United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-8"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership_Fellows_Program">Leadership Fellows Program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Leadership Fellows Program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Leadership Fellows Program is a fully funded event in which thirty Alpha Kappa Alpha Sorority sophomore and junior undergraduate members worldwide are individually trained for professional leadership roles. In addition, the fellows contribute to community service for one week. One of the selection criteria is that members must have at least a 3.0 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPA" title="GPA">GPA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leaders_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-leaders-120">[119]</a></sup> The program initially was planned in 1978. In the following year, the first program was held in <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a> with twenty-nine students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-9"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup> Various cities around the United States have held the Leadership Fellows Program. In the past, Alpha Kappa Alpha has sponsored the event through the Educational Advancement Foundation. Also, the program has been financed by <a href="/wiki/Pillsbury_Company" title="Pillsbury Company">Pillsbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyson_Foods" title="Tyson Foods">Tyson Foods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson" title="Johnson &amp; Johnson">Johnson &amp; Johnson</a>, and most recently <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-applicationleaders_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-applicationleaders-121">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-generalelectric_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-generalelectric-122">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships_in_Mathematics_and_Science">Partnerships in Mathematics and Science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Partnerships in Mathematics and Science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Partnerships in Mathematics and Science (PIMS) began in Eva Evans's administration in 1994, and was a part of the SPIRIT program during the <a href="/wiki/Linda_White" title="Linda White">Linda White</a> administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcnealey152_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-mcnealey152-124">[123]</a></sup> Eva Evans mentioned the need for a math and science program, "As a college sorority, we've always advanced an educational agenda. We always had high GPA requirements. And more than ever, we're pushing the importance of math and science for our girls. We need more black women in those fields."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-log2_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-log2-125">[124]</a></sup> The program's purpose is to increase the successes of youth in mathematics and science, as well as technology. Campaigns to highlight the program's importance were sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> and historically black colleges from across the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcnealey152_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-mcnealey152-124">[123]</a></sup> Several chapters provided two-week math and science summer camps on college and day school campuses, which consisted of hands-on-learning through laboratory interactions, field trips to important sites, youth camps, and speeches from influential experts in specific areas of studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-10"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey153_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey153-57">[57]</a></sup> For example, a PIMS program at Park Street Elementary School in <a href="/wiki/Marietta,_Georgia" title="Marietta, Georgia">Marietta, Georgia</a>, consisted of third through fifth grade girls and provided educational field trips in order to stimulate involvement in math and science.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NI_114-3"><a href="#cite_note-NI-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marietta_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-marietta-126">[125]</a></sup> Also, a national P.I.M.S. Olympiad, deriving from knowledge of math and science, in conjunction with the PIMS Community Parade was held at the 58th Boulé in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas, Texas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-11"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNealey153_57-3"><a href="#cite_note-McNealey153-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Young_Authors_Program">Young Authors Program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Kappa_Alpha&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Young Authors Program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Linda White's administrations, the Young Authors Program was born. The purpose of the program is to encourage and raise involvement in reading and writing in kindergarten through third grade school children. Each of the ten regions in the sorority had the opportunity to choose a child's story to be published in a two volume anthology entitled, <i>The Spirit Within: Voices of Young Authors</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-12"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup> In 2004, twenty children were honored in the first anthology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jet_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jet-127">[126]</a></sup> The authors were recognized and performed book signings in the 2004 and 2006 Boulés.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-programs_32-13"><a href="#cite_note-programs-32">[32]</a></sup> At the 2004 Boulé in <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville, Tennessee</a>, former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Education" title="United States Department of Education">Department of Education</a> Secretary <a href="/wiki/Rod_Paige" title="Rod Paige">Rod Paige</a> attended. On July 15, 2004, First Lady <a href="/wiki/Laura_Bush" title="Laura Bush">Laura Bush</a> spoke on the Ivy AKAdemy's dedication to reading initiatives, "Teaching our children to read is the most critical educational priority facing our country. Children who do not learn to read by third grade continue to find reading a challenge throughout their lives. These expectations increase in amount and complexity each year."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jet_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jet-127">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LauraBush_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-LauraBush-128">[127]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0">
<div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;text-align:center;">Sports</div>
<div class="NavContent plainlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;border-top:1px solid #aaa;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;">
<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;border-collapse:collapse; border-spacing:0px; border:none; width:100%; margin:0px; font-size:100%; clear:none; float:none">
